Row[2] = 90-yo sharp white female who woke up at 4:30 three mornings ago with right-sided facial paralysis and woke up her sister to show her.  They went to the ER and, of course, there was a concern for stroke.  She being 90 years old, so she was transferred to Mount Carmel for neurologic evaluation and stroke workup.  Initial CT at Madison County was normal.  An MRI scan here showed just senescent changes, but no acute infarct or mass.  She has been extremely nontoxic here.  She has been a little bit hypertensive at times, but she is a very anxious lady.  Her blood work all came back pretty normal.  Her TSH is slightly elevated at 5.7 and I will defer that to her primary care provider, her hemoglobin A1c was normal.  Her hemoglobin was healthy.  Her blood sugars have been under good control.  We did orthostatics, they were not positive.  In the end, we are recommending prednisone and acyclovir for a week for the Bell's palsy.  We have offered her a prescription for Fioricet for her chronic persistent headaches and I think she did try this last night and felt that there was some relief.  The family was hoping that she would qualify for inpatient rehabilitation because apparently they think that she has been falling at home.  So, we got a Physical Therapy evaluation.  She actually did quite well with therapy and in the end the recommendation was intermittent support with ADLs, but they felt that she did not qualify for skilled nursing.  I will, however, set up home health care if the family chooses that this might be helpful just to make sure she is compliant on medications and to assess response to therapy.  Her face is still quite paralyzed and we have been using ocular lubrication and I wrote a prescription for this as well.  Especially, at night she should put some ointment in her eye and try to sleep on the other side of her face to avoid corneal abrasions.  She will be discharged home with HHC
